International Commercial Telegraph, June 9, Reuters Special Commercial Telegram - Gold and Silver

London Gold Price The London gold price today is 137 shillings and 8.5 pence, an increase of 4 pence compared to yesterday.

London Silver Bar The London silver market today has a spot price of 19 pence and 175, and a futures price of 19 pence and 8125, both the same as yesterday's price. India bought in the morning, and China sold slightly. The market closed quietly.

New York Silver Bar The silver market opened steadily today, and the sentiment was uncertain. People in the industry are still optimistic about the development in Washington. The opening price of forward contracts is 4 to 15 pounds higher than yesterday's closing price.

Bombay Silver Bar The Bombay silver market closed steadily. The spot price rose by 3 annas to 55 rupees and 5 annas. The July 6 futures price was 55 rupees and 6 annas. The August 4 futures price was 56 rupees and 8 annas.

Special Telegraph The Jardine Matheson & Co. received a special telegram from London stating that, according to the London Financial Times' visit to New York, the biggest reason for the strength or weakness of the New York securities market is the resurgence of inflation. It is now firmly predicted that the US Treasury Department will reduce the value of the US dollar in the coming weeks, this time to 50 cents. There is also a rumor on Wall Street that Germany's financial situation is now very difficult, and France may also abandon the gold standard, and the exchange value of the British pound will also be reduced. The US dollar is in this position and cannot support itself. In addition, there is another reason, that is, the US government needs more funds to carry out its recovery program. If the value of the US dollar is reduced to 50 cents, 140 billion yuan can be obtained.

Exchange Rates

British-American The London foreign exchange market was very quiet this morning. The British-American exchange rate opened at $5.0637, the same as yesterday's closing rate for American-British exchange. There were slight fluctuations in the morning. The closing price was $5.061875, 1875 lower than the opening price. Also, one US dollar equals 3 shillings, 11 pence, and 413 British gold.

British-French The opening price was 76 francs 53, 3 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price. At 11 o'clock, it fell 7 pounds to 76 francs 46, and then changed.

American-British The opening price of the American-British exchange rate today was $5.06375, the same as yesterday's closing price, rising 125 to $5.065. This is the latest price.

American-French The opening price of the American-French exchange rate was 6.61 and 3/4, the same as yesterday's closing price.

Cotton and Wheat

Indian Cotton The Bombay cotton market experienced selling by speculators and buying by Japanese merchants this morning. The market closed steadily. The price of White Rose cotton for July-August was 210 rupees and a half, down one rupee.

British Cotton The closing price of Liverpool cotton for July was 6.33, up one pound from yesterday's closing price.

British Wheat The closing price of Liverpool wheat for July was 4 shillings and 9.5 pence, up 75.

American Cotton After the cotton market opened, brokers, bankers, and Europeans bought in, so the price rose slightly.

American Wheat Today's wheat market prices rose sharply, and there were few sellers.

Rubber

London The London rubber market closed steadily today. The transaction price for July-September was 6 pence 615, the same as yesterday's price.

New York The New York rubber market opened steadily today and showed a trend of turning stronger due to slightly broader demand. The absorption of profit-taking led to good market sentiment.

Securities

There is a possibility of slight profit-taking in the market, which may lead to mixed market conditions. However, the hope that the steel industry strike can be reversed and that Congress will adjourn soon is the reason for maintaining market sentiment. Disarmament Ends Temporarily, World Situation Takes a Sharp Turn: Italian, German, French, and British Leaders to Meet Separately; Little Entente Officially Recognizes Soviet Russia; Proposal for a Pacific Non-Aggression Pact

(Geneva) The General Disarmament Commission decided today to adjourn for several months. The general situation is changing rapidly. German Chancellor Hitler has agreed to meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Venice early next week to discuss the League of Nations and disarmament issues. This will have a significant impact on modern European history. French Foreign Minister Barthou has also accepted Prime Minister Mussolini's invitation to hold a similar meeting in Rome in early July. Meanwhile, Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov held lengthy meetings with the foreign ministers of Czechoslovakia, Romania, and Yugoslavia. Significant progress has been made on the issue of the Little Entente recognizing Soviet Russia, and the balance of power in Europe is about to undergo major changes. After meeting with the Little Entente countries, Litvinov also held an important dinner meeting with U.S. Special Envoy Davis to discuss the Soviet Russian proposal for a non-aggression pact among Pacific nations. (Ninth National Telegram)

(London) The Disarmament Conference has now entered a more pleasant phase. The focus of European political interest has shifted to the upcoming meeting between Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and German Chancellor Hitler. According to a Reuters dispatch from Berlin, negotiations between the dictators of Italy and Germany have been going on for some time, but Rome has flatly denied this, saying that Italy has not received any proposal from Germany for a meeting with the Italian Prime Minister. A Reuters dispatch from Berlin also stated that the location and time of the German-Italian meeting will be decided soon. At the same time, a Reuters correspondent in Geneva telephoned England, reportedly saying that French Foreign Minister Barthou had heard from Italian Prime Minister Mussolini that the Italian Prime Minister would meet Hitler in Venice in the middle of next week. The Italian Prime Minister also asked Barthou if he could visit Rome before or after Hitler's visit to Italy. It is said that the French Foreign Minister replied with vague remarks. (Ninth Reuters Dispatch)

Rome learned today from reliable sources that German Chancellor Hitler and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will meet in Venice on Monday or Tuesday. This is a historically significant meeting that will mark an era. Chancellor Hitler will fly from Berlin to Venice on Sunday. The official announcement of this matter has not yet been made, in fact, officials from the Foreign Ministries of Rome and Berlin are even denying it. However, the responsible party told the Associated Press that the meeting was invited by Prime Minister Mussolini and agreed to by Chancellor Hitler. Diplomats view this meeting as related to Germany's return to the League of Nations, its renewed participation in the Disarmament Conference, and Mussolini's last-ditch effort to salvage the Disarmament Conference. (Ninth National Telegram)

Rome, according to a Geneva dispatch, the Italian government has expressed to the French and German governments that it hopes that the responsible politicians of Italy, France, and Germany will choose a suitable location to meet with each other. The meeting place may be the Italian city of Venice. Although this news has not been officially confirmed, it echoes the news of the imminent meeting between Mussolini and Hitler. If the exchange of views between the Italian and German leaders is realized, its content will not be of a secret nature. France will also participate, but whether the form of participation will be direct or indirect is still unknown. (Eighth Havas Dispatch)

(Berlin) Chancellor Hitler's plan to visit Italy has materialized in an instant. Hitler will travel to Venice, Italy, with Foreign Minister Neurath in the middle of next week for a two-day stay. This will be Hitler's first formal visit abroad since taking office. (Ninth Havas Dispatch)

News from Rome and Berlin says that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini will soon meet with German Chancellor Hitler. This news has not yet been confirmed, but it is said that there is no impossibility of it happening. Mussolini is currently vacationing at his private residence near Pelledarbyvo City and will return to the capital this Sunday to watch the final of the World Football Championship between Italy and Czechoslovakia. After the event, he will leave the capital and return to the province. It is rumored that Mussolini may meet with Hitler in the province. (Eighth Havas Dispatch)

(Geneva) British Prime Minister MacDonald has instructed Eden to invite French Foreign Minister Barthou to meet in London. The British Prime Minister believes that since the two countries were able to work together harmoniously on the disarmament issue in Geneva recently, it is necessary for Barthou to visit London, as Barthou's visit to England can make the relationship between the two countries even closer. Barthou has agreed to go to London in early July. (Eighth Havas Dispatch)

(Geneva) French Foreign Minister Barthou officially announced to French reporters tonight that he has accepted the invitation of British Prime Minister MacDonald and will visit London in early July, departing from Paris around June 30. After arriving in England, he will meet with Prime Minister MacDonald and Foreign Secretary Simon. This trip is not only a return visit but will also involve special negotiations. (Eighth National Telegram)

(Paris) It was announced today that French Foreign Minister Barthou has accepted the invitation to meet with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Rome in early July. The meeting between Barthou and Mussolini will take place after the important meeting between Mussolini and Hitler. It is said that Mussolini intends to mediate between France and Germany to enable Germany to return to the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference. Before going to Rome, Barthou plans to go to London first to discuss disarmament and other issues with Prime Minister MacDonald and Foreign Secretary Simon. (Ninth National Telegram)

(London) It was announced here today that French Foreign Minister Barthou will visit London in the first week of July. The French Foreign Minister's visit here is at the invitation of British Prime Minister MacDonald. It is widely believed that the two will discuss disarmament and war debt issues during their meeting. The French Foreign Minister received the British Prime Minister's invitation in Geneva and telegraphed his acceptance of the invitation to visit England before departing for Paris last night. (Ninth Reuters Dispatch)

(Paris) According to a dispatch from Prague today, the Little Entente has recognized Soviet Russia. (Ninth Reuters Dispatch)

Little Entente Recognizes Soviet Russia: Capital of Czechoslovakia

According to well-informed sources and verified in Geneva, the foreign ministers of the three Little Entente countries jointly decided in Geneva to immediately recognize Soviet Russia de jure. Yesterday, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu and Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov, and Czech Foreign Minister Beneš and Litvinov, exchanged letters of mutual recognition. These letters will be published simultaneously in the capitals of Czechoslovakia and Romania, and in Moscow tonight. In addition, Yugoslavia will follow suit later and recognize the Soviet Union in the same way. (Ninth Havas Dispatch)

(Geneva) The meeting between Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov and the foreign ministers of the Little Entente countries on the issue of recognition did not end until 1:00 a.m. this morning. In addition to Litvinov, those who participated in the round table meeting included Czech Foreign Minister Beneš, Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, and Yugoslav Foreign Minister Jevtic. The conditions for recognition by Czechoslovakia and Romania have been agreed upon. However, regarding Yugoslavia, there are still some minor points of contention to be resolved. It is believed that if a complete agreement cannot be reached at this meeting, the Little Entente's recognition of Soviet Russia will have to wait until after the Little Entente's conference in Bucharest in late June. (Ninth National Telegram)

Disarmament Temporarily Improved; Crisis Has Been Averted; Committee to Be Formed Tomorrow

The perilous situation of the London Disarmament Conference has been averted. The General Commission met today in an atmosphere of peace and friendship and immediately passed the compromise proposal agreed upon by the chief representatives of Britain, France, and the United States. The proposal included: (1) Reaffirming that the conclusion of a general convention is the most urgent task; (2) Stipulating the procedures for immediate work to achieve this goal; (3) Recognizing the necessity of Germany's return to the conference. With the passage of this proposal by the General Commission, the work of the Disarmament Conference has made significant progress. The General Commission then announced the adjournment of the meeting until 3:30 p.m. on Monday next week, at which time two special committees will be formed, one to consider the issue of European regional security agreements and the other to consider the issue of guarantees for the implementation and supervision of the convention.

Before the proposal was passed, British representative Eden emphasized the importance of maintaining the traditional friendship between Britain and France and said that the cooperation of several major powers is indispensable, but the current environment is very difficult because they are not participating in the conference. However, a compromise has now been reached under these difficult circumstances. Britain's view of Germany's withdrawal from the Disarmament Conference has remained unchanged, and it deeply feels that since Germany's withdrawal from the conference, disarmament and international understanding have been greatly damaged. It hopes that the German government will return to the conference in an improved atmosphere of understanding to engage in the work that has been jointly undertaken for nearly two years.

Russian representative Litvinov's attitude today was very moderate, and his harmonious spirit surprised the representatives of various countries. Litvinov said that the Soviet Union has never opposed any point in the proposal, and he hopes that the Soviet Union's concept of a peace conference will always exist in the document archives of various countries' cabinets. The soldiers of the Red Army are actually the most peace-loving people in the world. Russia vows to work together with all nations and governments to achieve world peace.

Italian representative Soragna and Polish representative Raczyński both made reservations. The Italian representative stated that unless the political issues are resolved, he fears that the Disarmament Conference may not make appropriate progress. Litvinov was also not entirely satisfied with the proposal, so he did not vote when the proposal was formally presented.

The main representatives are returning to their countries tonight, so the unprecedented storms of the Disarmament Conference have temporarily calmed down. (Eighth Reuters Dispatch)

(Geneva) Since the Davis Compromise was reached, the prospects for disarmament are much more optimistic, and the crisis of the conference breaking down seems to have passed for the time being. The resolution passed by the General Commission clearly indicates that the invitation to Germany to return to the seat is due to the mediation of the U.S. representative. It is reported that the British delegation had received instructions from London beforehand, stating that if there was no room left for continued talks with Germany, there was no need to proceed with the conference. The Italian delegation also held the same attitude. The Davis proposal accommodates France's claims on the one hand, referring the two major issues of security and disarmament to the committees for continued discussion, and on the other hand, stipulating that the General Assembly should adjourn to await the outcome of the invitation to Germany to return before reconvening. Therefore, this resolution made a clear provision for inviting Germany. This case is said to have been distributed to the governments of participating countries for filing. The Disarmament Conference may adjourn for two or three months to facilitate the negotiation of a Franco-German compromise and to contact Germany to return to the League of Nations. Therefore, the Disarmament Conference may be extended for several months. (Eighth National Telegram)

(Geneva) The General Disarmament Commission passed the Davis proposal today, stipulating an indefinite adjournment. During the adjournment period, the four committees will continue to study various disarmament proposals and conduct negotiations on Germany's return to the conference. On Monday afternoon, the General Commission will reconvene to begin establishing the four committees in the Davis proposal. This proposal has been unanimously accepted by France and Britain. Experts commented on this proposal, saying that an agreement has been reached on the issue of future disarmament, but it still hides the huge gaps between Britain, France, Germany, and Italy on fundamental issues. It is still unknown whether the alliance between France and Russia will worsen Anglo-French relations, making it difficult for the country to return to the League of Nations. When the General Commission reconvenes this term, representatives from various countries will strive to be selected for the committees and then quietly adjourn until October, and then decide whether to advance or retreat depending on the situation of the contacts with Germany. It is noteworthy that Japan did not participate in the secret deliberations yesterday or today. The General Commission met at 4:10 p.m. this afternoon and adjourned at 6:10 p.m. French Foreign Minister Barthou proposed the Davis proposal next Monday. Barthou insisted that France hopes that Germany will automatically return to Geneva. Barthou said, "We let Germany act freely. If Germany closes its door, we cannot open it. Only Germany can open this door. We do not want to pursue a policy of blockade, this is not the doctrine we hold." Davis declared that this case is of great contribution to European peace. Davis said, "This case has not resolved all the issues of disarmament, but it has changed the atmosphere of the conference from disappointment to genuine hope." Soviet Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov supported this case, saying that there was nothing to oppose. Litvinov also hoped that his proposal for a non-aggression pact and the restructuring of the Disarmament Conference into a peace conference would no longer be shelved by diplomats and could be revisited for discussion. Six neutral countries also expressed their acceptance. (Eighth National Telegram)

Attitudes of Various Countries' Representatives: Soviet Russia Also Supports Compromise Proposal; Italy and Hungary Reserve; Austria Does Not Express

(Geneva) The General Commission of the Disarmament Conference met at 4:15 p.m. today. French Foreign Minister Barthou explained the compromise proposal agreed upon by him, Eden, and Davis, praising the contributions of the British and American representatives. Regarding Germany's return to the Disarmament Conference, Barthou said that although the resolution mentions Germany's return to the Disarmament Conference, discussions on this matter should be proposed and conducted by the governments of various countries. Germany's return to Geneva is not crucial to the disarmament issue but must be done freely and without coercion. Regarding the Soviet Union's proposal to transform the Disarmament Conference into a "Permanent Conference for the Guarantee of Peace," Barthou believes that it is of far-reaching significance but should not cause the Disarmament Conference to lose its original mission. British representative Eden expressed his sincere gratitude to Barthou and Davis.

In particular, Eden said that Barthou's remarks on Anglo-French relations were deeply felt. Eden said that the draft resolution proves the solidarity of Anglo-French relations. Britain is eager for the Disarmament Conference to achieve results and is unwilling to engage in empty discussions for a long time. For this reason, it accepts the compromise proposal agreed upon by the representatives of the three countries and hopes that the atmosphere of the Disarmament Conference will be refreshed and that Germany will also return to Geneva. Germany's withdrawal from the Disarmament Conference caused the current difficulties and increased the danger to European peace, bearing considerable responsibility. With this compromise proposal, Germany can rejoin the work of disarmament. U.S. representative Davis said that countries must compromise with each other, so the United States also supports the new compromise proposal set by the representatives of the three countries. Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov said that the Soviet Union was not entirely satisfied with the compromise proposal, but it did not contain anything that would cause the Soviet representative to object. Swedish Foreign Minister Sandler spoke on behalf of six countries (Sweden, Switzerland, the Netherlands, Denmark, Norway, Spain), saying that he believed that the new compromise proposal set by the representatives of Britain, the United States, and France could help the Disarmament Conference and resolve it. Hungarian representative described his country's demands and made explicit reservations on the compromise proposal. Italian representative Surania reiterated his reservations to the presidium but also said that Italy is willing to continue to cooperate with various countries beyond formal and procedural issues in order to achieve a peaceful resolution to various major international issues. Bulgarian representative Migoff declared his support for the compromise proposal. The Austrian representative did not intend to express an opinion. Polish representative Rattesky said that the French compromise proposal eased the atmosphere of the conference and was deeply gratifying, and then reiterated his reservations to the presidium. Finally, the Persian representative spoke, and the compromise proposal was then passed by the General Commission without opposition. The 54 countries attending the Disarmament Conference, the General Commission is scheduled to meet on Monday afternoon to assign work. (Eighth Havas Dispatch)

Lithuania: Cabinet Submits Resignation; Military Coup Attempt Fails; 70 Arrested

The Lithuanian capital, the Tubelis Cabinet, submitted its resignation today because the garrison in the capital plotted a coup, intending to support former Prime Minister Voldemaras as dictator. (Ninth Reuters Dispatch)

Riga, as far as is known here, the coup in the Lithuanian capital has indeed been suppressed. The number of those arrested has reached 70. Chief of the Army General Staff Kubiliunas is also among them. (Eighth Reuters Dispatch)

The Lithuanian capital, Elta News Agency, released a message saying that the government has sent Damasauskas to organize a committee to determine the responsibility for the coup. Two military officers have been arrested, and the morale of the army has stabilized, and discipline has been restored. According to some sources, those who brewed the coup seemed to be directed by foreign countries. Fortunately, President Smetona and the government took a firm and calm stance, and the conspiracy failed. (Eighth Havas Dispatch)

Spanish Galicia: Independence Movement Revived; Opposes Land Law Strongly

The Catalan independence movement in Madrid has been going on for years. The initial intention was that the Spanish revolution had ended. Recently, because the Spanish government promulgated the land law, this movement has been revived. The chairman of Catalonia gave a speech today, saying that this law is absurd and dangerous, and it is an attack on Catalonia's autonomy. It is expected that the members of the Catalan province in the House of Representatives will all resign next week. (Ninth Reuters Dispatch)

U.S. Steel Industry: Labor-Management Dispute Likely to Be Resolved

(Washington) Government officials and labor-management representatives of the steel industry met until late at night today, seeking a compromise, so the labor-management dispute in the steel industry seems to have a chance of being resolved. All parties are sincere in seeking a solution to the methods of recognizing the union, strikes, and government monitoring of workers' elections. (Eighth National Telegram)

Japan's Concerns About Naval Conference: Does Not Propose to Cancel Treaty Itself; Repeated Hardline Propaganda Makes Britain and the United States Wary; Now Advocates for Conference to Be Held in Paris

(Tokyo) Japan's attitude toward the issue of whether the Washington Naval Treaty should be canceled is most noteworthy. It is reported that Britain and the United States have held preliminary naval military conferences because they expected Japan to propose the cancellation of the treaty. However, the opinion of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in the capital believes that Japan does not currently need to notify the cancellation first. Because if a new treaty can be concluded at the next disarmament conference, the Washington Treaty will naturally be eliminated. However, if the conference breaks down, notifying the cancellation will not be a missed opportunity. This issue has also become a research topic in France. Japan is paying attention to what attitude France will take. (According to Article 23 of the Washington Treaty, any country that wants to cancel this treaty must notify two years before the expiration date of this treaty, December 31, 1936, that is, before December 31 of this year). (Ninth Japan United Press Telegram)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, regarding the issue of procedures for the next disarmament at the initial discussion of the London Disarmament Preliminary Negotiations, has contacted the Navy and decided on the following main points. Foreign Minister Hirota telegraphed to Ambassador Matsudaira in Britain, Ambassador Saito in the United States, and Ambassador Sato in France, and Ambassador Sugimura in Italy yesterday, instructing them to negotiate with the governments of various countries with the following purpose: (1) The Imperial Government advocates that the next disarmament conference be held in Paris, because naval disarmament has always been held in Washington, Geneva, and London. This time, Paris is considered appropriate. After Ambassador Sato obtains the recognition of the French government, Ambassador Matsudaira will propose it as an issue for preliminary negotiations. (2) The opening date of the conference is appropriate in April of this year when the London Treaty is revised. (3) The agenda of the next disarmament conference is limited to the relationship of the Washington and London Treaties, and absolutely opposes mentioning political issues, especially the Far East issues. (Ninth Electric Communications Telegram)

White House Banquet for Count Konoe: President Roosevelt Expresses: Willing to Meet with Japanese Political Leaders in Honolulu

(Washington) President Roosevelt hosted a banquet at the White House today to entertain Count Konoe, Speaker of the Japanese House of Peers. According to Japanese people who attended the banquet, President Roosevelt expressed that when he travels to the Hawaiian Islands, he is willing to meet with a delegation of Japanese politicians in Honolulu. It is learned that Japanese newspapers have advocated that this meeting is enough to show goodwill in the Pacific before the naval conference. Those who attended today's White House banquet included Japanese Ambassador to the United States Saito, Secretary of State Hull, Secretary of the Treasury Morgenthau, and Senator Pittman. Most of them are American and Japanese leaders. (Eighth National Telegram)

British Colonies Boycott Japanese Goods: Malaya Implements Import Permit System; Jamaica, West Indies Increases Import Taxes

(Tokyo) According to a telegram from Consul General Tamura in Singapore to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Straits Settlements decided to implement the import permit system from the 11th. Anyone who wants to obtain this permit must report the import amount from January of last year to March of this year, by type and industry, and the merchant ships carrying them. According to a survey by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, after the implementation of this system, Japanese goods will be sharply reduced by an average of 60%. Other countries will not be so severely affected. In fact, this is differential treatment for Japanese goods, so it is clearly a violation of the most-favored-nation clause. Consul General Tamura called attention to the Straits Settlements government on the 8th. (Ninth Electric Communications Telegram)

The Kingston Jamaican government today promulgated a tariff on Japanese cotton and raw silk that is close to a ban, with a tax rate of 12.5 cents to 25 cents per yard. This tax rule took effect on May 7. Tax evaders will be fined $2,500. This action is based on the policy announced by Commerce Minister Remessman to restrict the import of Japanese textiles into the territory. (Eighth National Telegram)

(Geneva) It is reported that Italy has agreed to comply with the proposal of the Song International to prohibit the supply of arms to Bolivia and Paraguay in South America, but only on the condition that Japan also complies with this measure. However, Japan has indicated that since it has withdrawn from the League of Nations, it cannot cooperate with the League under Article 3 of the Covenant. It is also reported that Italy's compliance with this ban is subject to another condition, namely that the ban shall not apply to existing orders. This condition will make the ban difficult to implement. (Reuter, 8th)

(Geneva) The Council of the League of Nations sought the agreement of various countries on the issue of prohibiting arms shipments to Bolivia and Paraguay in South America. It was also stated that Japan has no arms shipments to Bolivia and Paraguay and has never transported them in fact. It is noted that the Council of the League of Nations originally intended to establish an agreement to obtain the consent of all countries in order to implement the embargo. Now that Japan's reply is as such, this hope has been dashed. It is further noted that Italy has made a reservation on this matter, stating that Italy will only participate in the ban if both Japan and Russia participate. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Bans Strange and Bizarre Women's Clothing; Jiangxi Provincial Government Formulates Measures to Crack Down, Starting with Female Civil Servants

Nanchang dispatch: Chairman Chiang Kai-shek believes that the clothing of women in the city recently has become increasingly strange and bizarre, not only hindering hygiene but also harming public morals. At this time of implementing the New Life Movement, it should be corrected in a timely manner. He has specially ordered the provincial government to formulate measures to crack down on it. After receiving the order, the provincial government has already formulated measures to crack down on strange and bizarre women's clothing and ordered the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau and relevant departments to be informed. The measures obtained are recorded below:

Chapter 1: General Provisions. 1. These measures are specifically formulated to crack down on strange and bizarre women's clothing that harms public morals and is unhygienic. 2. Dimensions specified in these measures shall be based on the city foot.

Chapter 2: Clothing. 3. Clothing is divided into two types: qipao and short jacket. The length and size shall be based on the following: (1) The longest qipao must be one inch from the back of the foot. (2) The highest collar must be one and a half inches from the jawbone. (3) The shortest sleeve length must reach the elbow joint. (4) Side slits on the qipao must not exceed three inches above the knee. The short jacket must not show the waistband of the trousers. (5) All those wearing short jackets must wear skirts. Those who do not wear skirts must have their clothing cover three inches below the buttocks. (6) The waist must not be tightly fitted to the body and must be slightly loose. (7) The shortest trouser length must be four inches below the knee, and legs must not be exposed and bare feet must not be worn, but this does not apply when engaging in labor. (8) The shortest skirt length must be four inches below the knee. 4. Those wearing Western-style clothing must refer to the provisions of Article 3 for length and size.

Chapter 3: Attire. 5. Hair must be neatly combed and drooping behind the head. Hair length must not extend below the neckline. Women with long hair may wear a bun. 6. Foot-binding and breast-binding are prohibited. 7. Short jackets made of wool or without buttons are prohibited. 8. It is forbidden to wear pajamas and undershirts or slippers and walk barefoot in the streets.

Chapter 4: Implementation Measures. 9. The implementation of these measures will start in Nanchang City first. The implementation period is as follows: (1) Female civil servants, female teachers, female students, and family members of male civil servants must implement it after half a month. (2) Women from other sectors must implement it after one month. 10. The Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau shall copy these measures and prepare leaflets to be distributed door-to-door. 11. Women whose clothing and attire do not comply with these measures shall be interfered with by the patrol police. Those who resist may be detained and punished. (June 7th)

Provisional Regulations on Summary Criminal Procedure Draft

The Executive Yuan, according to the Ministry of Judicial Administration's report, states that in recent years, criminal cases in various provinces have increased, and in view of the central and local financial situation, it has not been possible to drastically increase the number of judicial officials, resulting in backlogs of cases in various courts and county governments that also handle judicial affairs. Defendants are detained for long periods pending trial, causing endless suffering. The Ministry, as its duty, has to seek remedies. Previously, it was considered that the procedures prescribed by the current Criminal Procedure Law were too cumbersome and should be amended to facilitate proceedings. A draft was prepared and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation. However, the promulgation of the new law will still take time, and it is urgent to first establish a method for current emergency use. Therefore, a draft of 22 articles of the Provisional Regulations on Summary Criminal Procedure was drafted and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and submission to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and passage, and then promulgated as a separate regulation. It was submitted to the 162nd meeting of the Executive Yuan, which resolved to "pass it and send it to the Central Political Conference." It was also submitted to the 410th meeting of the Political Conference, which resolved to send it to the Legislative Yuan. On the 8th, the Legislative Yuan meeting resolved to send it to the Criminal Law Committee for review. The original draft terms are recorded below:

Article 1: In cases listed in Article 8 of the Criminal Procedure Law, if the court of first instance determines that the defendant's confession during the investigation or other existing evidence is sufficient to establish their guilt, it may, upon the prosecutor's request, impose a sentence directly by order without going through the ordinary trial procedure. The sentence imposed by the order referred to in the preceding paragraph shall be limited to imprisonment of not more than six months, detention, or a fine. Article 2: When investigating cases listed in Article 8 of the Criminal Procedure Law, if the prosecutor considers it appropriate to impose a sentence by order, they shall immediately make a request in writing. The provisions of Article 218 of the Criminal Procedure Law shall apply mutatis mutandis to the request referred to in the preceding paragraph. The request in the first paragraph shall have the same effect as prosecution. Article 3: If the court considers that a case for which the prosecutor requests a sentence by order should not or cannot be sentenced by order, it shall apply the ordinary trial procedure. Article 4: Except in special circumstances, the court shall immediately dispose of a case for which the prosecutor requests a sentence by order. Article 5: The sentencing order shall record the following matters in a concise manner: 1. The defendant's name, age, occupation, address, or residence; 2. The facts of the crime; 3. The applicable provisions of the law; 4. The matters listed in each paragraph of Article 323 of the Criminal Procedure Law; 5. The court and date of the sentencing order; 6. A notice that a formal trial may be requested within five days from the date of service of the sentencing order. The sentencing order shall be signed by the presiding judge who issued the order.

Article 6: After receiving the original of the sentencing order, the clerk shall immediately prepare a copy and serve it on the parties. Article 7: The defendant may request a formal trial within five days after the service of the sentencing order. The request referred to in the preceding paragraph shall be made in writing to the court that issued the sentencing order. Article 8: The defendant may waive the right to request a formal trial. If a request has been made, it may be withdrawn before the judgment of the first instance. The waiver of the right to request a formal trial and the withdrawal of the request shall be made in writing to the court that issued the sentencing order, but may be made orally on the trial date or when questioned. If the defendant waives the right to request a formal trial or withdraws the request, they shall lose their right to request. Article 9: The provisions of Article 365 of the Criminal Procedure Law shall apply mutatis mutandis to the request for a formal trial and the waiver or withdrawal of the request. Article 10: If the court considers that the procedure for requesting a formal trial violates the regulations, it shall dismiss it by ruling. An appeal may be made against the ruling referred to in the preceding paragraph within five days. Article 11: If the court considers that the request for a formal trial is legal, it shall try the case in accordance with the ordinary procedure and shall not be bound by the sentencing order. Article 12: If the defendant, after being legally summoned on the date of the formal trial, fails to appear in court without a legitimate reason, the court may dismiss their request by judgment without conducting an investigation. Article 13: After the court renders a judgment in accordance with the request for a formal trial, the sentencing order shall lose its effect. Article 14: A sentencing order shall have the same effect as a final judgment after the period for requesting a formal trial has expired, or the defendant has waived the right to request, withdrawn the request, or the ruling dismissing the request has become final. Article 15: In cases listed in Article 8 of the Criminal Procedure Law, after a judicial police officer investigates and transfers the case to the prosecutor, if the prosecutor considers it unnecessary to conduct further investigation, they may directly prosecute or request a sentence by order based on the results of the investigation by the judicial police officer, but the suspect who has been transferred shall still be questioned. Article 16: In cases listed in Article 8 of the Criminal Procedure Law, if the prosecutor of the court of first instance considers it unnecessary to appear in court on the trial date, they may not appear in court, but shall notify the court before the date. In the case referred to in the preceding paragraph, the matters stated in the written statement submitted by the prosecutor shall be read aloud in court by the judge or clerk, or the judge shall inform them of the gist of the statement in lieu of the prosecutor's statement. Article 17: If the court of first instance is aware of imprisonment of not more than six months, detention, or a fine in cases listed in Article 8 of the Criminal Procedure Law, the judgment may record the defendant's name, the main text of the judgment, the facts of the crime, and the applicable provisions of the law in a concise manner, and the judge shall sign it and deliver the original to the defendant in court at the time of the pronouncement. If the prosecutor or private prosecutor requests it, it shall also be delivered together. In the case referred to in the preceding paragraph, the appeal period shall be calculated from the date of delivery of the original to the defendant. After the delivery of the original referred to in the first paragraph, if a party files an appeal, a formal judgment shall be prepared and served on the parties, and the same shall apply to those who request the service of a formal judgment within five days after the pronouncement of the judgment, but this shall not affect the application of the provisions of the preceding paragraph. Article 18: The court may render a judgment of dismissal, non-acceptance, or lack of jurisdiction without oral argument. Article 19: In cases where the court considers that detention or a fine should be imposed or a judgment of innocence should be pronounced, if the defendant, after being legally summoned, fails to appear in court without a legitimate reason, the court may render a judgment without waiting for their statement. Article 20: After the pronouncement of a judgment imposing detention or a fine, if the defendant agrees, the prosecutor may immediately direct the execution in court. If the prosecutor is not present in court, the judge may immediately direct it. Article 21: These regulations shall apply mutatis mutandis to county judicial offices and county governments that also handle judicial affairs. In the circumstances of Article 1, county judicial offices and county governments that also handle judicial affairs may impose sentences by order ex officio. Article 22: These regulations shall come into effect from the date of promulgation.

Shantou Salt Police Open Fire, Causing Trouble; Arrest and Beat Patrol Police for Investigating Smuggled Salt; One of Chen Weizhou's Achievements

Shantou correspondence: After the salt affairs system in Chaozhou was reformed, Chen Weizhou, the Salt Transport Envoy of Guangdong and Guangxi, immediately sent hundreds of salt police officers to station in the coastal salt-producing counties. Carrying new and sharp firearms, they went everywhere in groups of three or five to search people's houses. If salt was found, it was treated as smuggling, and they were arrested and heavily fined. People feared them like tigers. For example, salt police officers in Huilai County pulled out the numbered bamboo sticks inserted by the Field Measurement Office in the fields. When the field measurer came forward to dissuade them, they refused to comply and were beaten and seriously injured. For example, on the afternoon of the 3rd, salt police officers in Shantou City suddenly searched for smuggled salt in the homes of residents on Zhaoshang Street. Because they did not consult with the police and carried guns into people's homes to overturn boxes and cabinets, the patrol police came forward to intervene. The salt police officers were furious and accused the patrol police of protecting smugglers. They arrested the patrol police officers, beat them severely, and detained them in the salt sales office at the Chaozhou Bridge. The sales office is located at the light railway station on Zhongma Road, and Zhaoshang Street is under the jurisdiction of the Fourth Public Security Bureau. The Fourth Public Security Bureau is located in the alley opposite the sales office. When the patrol police officer was arrested, the Fourth Public Security Bureau knew about it. They came forward to negotiate unsuccessfully. At that time, a salt inspector was in the alley, and the Fourth Public Security Bureau arrested him in retaliation. This happened at 4 PM on the 3rd. As a result, both sides were on high alert. At about 6 PM, both sides took hostile actions, and gunfire broke out. It lasted for an hour. As a result, a policeman of the Fourth Public Security Bureau was killed, and all the policemen scattered from the roofs. Later, the Public Security Bureau sent security teams, detective teams, and formal garrison troops to open fire to stop the salt police officers at the sales office. The salt police captain was arrested, and the salt police guns were confiscated. The storm then subsided. At that time, the citizens did not know the truth. They suddenly heard gunfire and mistakenly thought that enemy troops had invaded Shantou. They were all frightened because rumors had been rampant in recent days. After the citizens understood the situation, they all deeply hated the power of the salt police. (4th)

The Rampant Bandit Situation in Chaozhou and Meizhou

Shantou Correspondence: The bandit gangs in Chaozhou and Meizhou have recently become restless again. A large group of soldiers recently gathered in the deep and densely forested areas of the Eight Villages Mountains, Monkey Slide Rock, and Nine Dragon Zhang in Fengshun County, stretching for forty to fifty miles. These fellows are exceptionally rampant, openly carrying guns and killing the chief of the Public Security Sub-bureau, the village head, and the county magistrate. Chen Jitang has specifically telegraphed Deng Longguang, the commander of the Independent Fourth Division, ordering him to lead troops to be responsible for suppressing them. The Chen Xin battalion regiment of the Independent Second Division stationed in Fengshun is also under Deng's command. The police guard teams, armed civilian militias, and reserve teams of the eight counties in Chaozhou and Meizhou are all subject to Deng's dispatch for forceful interception. Fengshun is a crucial military area in the Eastern River region, and new-style trenches have been dug in three layers around the city, with numerous artillery emplacements attached to the city walls. Chen Jitang has given Deng a deadline to completely pacify the remaining bandits within the county this month. The provincial government recently appointed Liang Guocai, an adjutant of the Seventh Division, as the magistrate of Fengshun County. Liang is from Songkou in Meixian. He arrived in Fengshun by car from Mei on the 31st of last month to take over the county seal and posted an announcement of his assumption of office on the 1st of this month. Banditry is rampant in Chaozhou and Meizhou, especially in Fengshun. On the morning of the 26th of last month, more than twenty bandits suddenly appeared at the Shuiwei area of Xintang Market, on the border of Meixian and Fengshun, carrying a machine gun and other weapons such as Browning pistols. They were spotted by a woman gathering firewood on the mountain. After she reported it to the reserve team, the team, consisting of twenty-two men, purely voluntary in nature, patrolled in shifts during the day and guarded the blockhouse at night. The squad leader, Zhang Guocai, upon receiving the report, went up the mountain to investigate and was immediately shot dead by the bandits. The cook, hearing the gunfire, immediately rushed to report to the Sixth Guard Company of Xintang Market and telegraphed the training office. By the time the troops were assembled, the Shuiwei blockhouse had been completely looted by the bandits, with a loss of twenty-two guns and thirteen hundred bullets. When the guard company arrived, the bandits had already fled towards Langdang Rock in Fengshun. On the 30th, the entire Sixth Guard Company of the Training Office moved into Tou Mountain in Fengshun to search and suppress the Yangqian Pit area. This area fell into communist control during the year 1929. In 1930, it was pacified by Zhang Da's troops. Now, the remnants of the bandit areas everywhere are all stirring restlessly, spreading rumors and posting reactionary slogans. The bandit situation in Chaozhou and Meizhou is so rampant that it urgently awaits a large-scale military suppression. (2nd)

Jiangsong: Frugal Administrative Expenses to Repair Sea Dams

The ninth administrative meeting of this county opened on the 7th and concluded today (the 9th), holding a closing ceremony. Regarding the case of the dangerous sea dams needing repair, the expenses are estimated to be about 80,000 yuan. In addition to 40,000 yuan being allocated from the provincial treasury, there is still a shortfall of 40,000 yuan. It was ordered that methods be found to raise the funds. County Magistrate Jin once convened a meeting of various agencies to discuss this, and the resolution was to:

Assume three methods for raising funds: (1) Set aside a proportion from the frugal savings of the administrative expenses in the local budget, (1) Collect a few percentage points from the fields, (1) Advise merchants to donate according to the standard of business tax. This has been submitted to the administrative meeting for discussion and resolved to hand it over to the finance team for review. This review report was submitted to the meeting for discussion today, and it was resolved to use frugal savings from local budget administrative expenses to supplement the funds.

Nanhui: A Bloody Armed Clash Occurs in Huangzhen

A bloody tragedy of an armed clash involving a crowd suddenly occurred in Huangzhen, in the first district of the county, at about 1:00 p.m. yesterday (the 8th). The cause of the incident was that Tang Yinlou, an engineer at the Zhongdinghe Hosiery Factory in the town, was seen by Yang Qiusheng, a local gangster, while he was harassing a female worker in a secluded spot a few days ago. Yang immediately reprimanded him, which led to an argument and then a physical fight. Yang, feeling humiliated, decided to gather his associates, including Zhu Xiaomao, to seek revenge. Yesterday morning, they quietly arrived in the town with knives, guns, and other weapons. Jiang Jinsong, a clerk in the town office, who knew Zhu, saw that he was leading a large group of people and inquired about the reason. Jiang, fearing that it would cause trouble, tried to dissuade them. By this time, both sides had gathered. After a disagreement, they immediately started fighting. Dozens of people were injured in the melee, and all the shops were in a panic and closed their doors. The town head, Yang Yaopu, heard the alarm and immediately telegraphed the Sixth Zao Bay First District Office, which relayed the message to the Public Security Bureau. The police team immediately dispatched many armed police officers to rush to the scene to suppress the situation, but the fighters had all fled. The seriously injured were carried to the public hospital for treatment. What was shocking about this clash was that even police officers from the Public Security Bureau participated in it. A Mauser pistol, three daggers, and an insignia were seized on the spot. The county government is thoroughly investigating the matter.

Five Family Members Heavily Suspected in the Wang Duosheng Murder Case

It has been reported yesterday that Wang Jinsheng, the temple keeper of Maoshan Palace outside Limen, was brutally murdered and his body dumped at the river dock. His wife, Mrs. Pan, his son, Genbao, his daughter, Zhangjin (also known as Changxin), and his fiancé, Chen Wanquan, are all suspected. It is now known that Wang Jinsheng disapproved of his fiancé, Chen Wanquan, causing discord between the couple. Wang's nephew, Pan Tiansheng, had recently come to Suzhou to live with Wang and was also detained after the incident. All of them have been sent to the court for questioning and detention. During the examination of the body, it was found that the deceased's scrotum had been cut into a fishnet-like shape with sharp scissors. A pair of scissors stained with blood was found in the deceased's home by the police, which is naturally considered the murder weapon. Furthermore, the fingernail marks on the deceased's abdomen matched his wife Mrs. Pan's hand when it was pressed against them. Also, Pan Tiansheng's shirt and pants were stained with blood. Therefore, although none of them have confessed, officials have determined that all five family members are heavily suspected.

Wuxi: Appeal Against Forced Service as Jia Head

Most cities and villages in the county are under the Yitu system. For silver tribute, a number of coins must be paid at once. The method is that each figure is divided into ten classes, which take turns serving annually. The one with the most fields serves as the head of the class. Zhu Quanfu, a villager from Caojia Alley in Figure 62 of the 15th District of the county, only paid 93.4 cents in silver tribute, while Zhu Jinfang in the same figure paid 2.277 yuan, Cao Juquan paid 1.796 yuan, and Zhu Xigou paid 1.658 yuan. There are several other households that paid 1.5 or 6 jiao. However, Tang Bingquan, the district chief of that district, reported to the county government, forcing Zhu Quanfu to serve as the head of the class and secretly allowing Zhu Jinfang, who should have served as the head of the class, to avoid it. The county government, without investigating, sent police to the village and summoned Zhu Quanfu to the county yesterday. Without asking for reasons, they immediately detained him. Now Zhu Quanfu's family members have appealed to all parties.

Another Dispute Arises in the Rice Industry in Wuxi

Five boats carrying soybeans from Changzhou, approximately 100,000 shi, arrived at the river in front of the Hengde Oil Factory in the west of Gongyun Bridge in our county a few days ago. While they were being unloaded, the Xinmao Rice and Grain Store in our county learned of this and believed that the Changzhou merchants were unloading goods across the border and seizing business, which not only disrupted the market but also violated ministerial regulations. (According to the tooth tax regulations, the rice and soybean business is divided into areas, each trading within its own boundaries. A trader who pays the tax in Area A cannot unload goods in Area B. This is customary.) They reported this to the Rice and Soybean Industry Association, requesting assistance. After receiving the report, the association sent representatives to advise the Changzhou merchants to stop unloading and invited Chen Jinli, the owner of the oil factory, to the association to discuss the matter. As a result, the Wuxi Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to invite representatives of the Changzhou Rice and Soybean Industry to Wuxi to discuss a solution. Yesterday, Lin Yibao, chairman of the Changzhou Rice and Soybean Industry Association, came to Wuxi from Changzhou to discuss mediation plans with Qian Sunqing and others at the county chamber of commerce. It was decided that until a solution is reached in this case, all goods already transported to Wuxi by Changzhou merchants should be stopped from unloading to avoid disputes. The Wuxi Rice Industry Association, fearing that the dispute would escalate, also submitted a report to the county government yesterday, requesting that the Public Security Bureau be ordered to send police to stop it.

Changzhou: Bandit Leader Lin Runlong Executed

Lin Runlong, the bandit leader from the Erweitai in Wuyi, had previously conspired with Zhu Fugen and others to rob the house of Shen Jingkou in the 19th District, and resisted and injured the victim, Shen Minghua. Xiaoshan: All Eastern Countryside Cocoon Markets Stop Weighing

Special Feature: Impressions of an Economic Survey in Guangxi Province (Continued) by Qian Jiaju

Let me talk about the mining industry in Fu He Zhong. "Fu He Zhong" is the general name for the three counties of "Fuchuan," "He County," and "Zhongshan," which is the most famous mining area in Guangxi. The Guangxi Construction Department has an office stationed in Xiwan, Zhongshan. Xiwan is about 30 miles away from Babu. The office has its own truck for transportation. Anyone who wants to visit can simply make a phone call, and the office will send a car to pick them up. The director of the office, Mr. Tao Shaoqin, is a German-educated student with extensive geological knowledge and mining experience. According to Mr. Tao, Fu He Zhong produces the most tin. There are no fewer than 400 large and small mining companies in total. However, except for two or three companies that use machinery for mining (He Cheng, Pu Yi, Bao Hua, these three companies), the rest use traditional methods. There are several types of traditional mining methods. One is called "Long Kou," which refers to tin ore located inside the mountains. To mine it, a tunnel must be dug from the mountain opening. If there is a water source inside the tunnel to wash the sand, it is called "Water Tunnel"; if there is no water source, it is called "Dry Tunnel" (tin sand must be washed with water, so water tunnels are better than dry tunnels). Another is called "Zhuang Tou," which refers to mining tin sand on the open ground. There are also "Water Zhuang" and "Dry Zhuang." Some of these traditional mining companies have a large capital of up to thousands of yuan, while others have as little as several hundred yuan. Local people often raise several hundred yuan, buy a piece of land, and start mining themselves. Wages are not counted. The mined tin sand is sold to companies that refine tin ore. Generally, 100 jin of tin sand can be sold for 120 to 130 yuan, and about 70 jin of pure tin can be refined. The cost of 100 jin of pure tin (including taxes) is about 210 yuan. It sells for 220 yuan in Babu, 240 yuan in Guangzhou, and 270 to 280 yuan in Hong Kong. In the past year or two, due to the high price of tin in Hong Kong, tin merchants have made substantial profits, so more and more people are mining, and the production of tin has also greatly increased. Among them, the shareholders of several large companies that use machinery for mining are mostly overseas Chinese who have returned from Southeast Asia. They were hit hard by the economic panic in the world and could not gain a foothold in Southeast Asia. Therefore, they turned their attention to investing in domestic industries. These overseas Chinese are truly admirable for their spirit and courage. They are mostly stout, wearing old-fashioned short Western suits, and carrying a cane, running around the mining area all day long. From this, we can tell that they are overseas Chinese businessmen who have built their wealth through diligence and frugality. However, their harsh treatment of workers is also shocking. The "Rules of Compliance for Miners" in the Pu Yi Shi Ren Company stipulates that "Five days of wages will be deducted from each worker's salary as a deposit. If they leave without notice, it will be confiscated." The Bao Hua Company stipulates in the "Treatment Rules for Miners" that "If a worker resigns without reason and has not worked for seven days, their wages may not be paid. If they die due to work, the factory will provide 10 yuan for funeral expenses and compensation equal to 100 days' wages." Speaking of the lives of the workers, they are truly worse off than prisoners in Beiping. They live in the most dilapidated and filthy dormitories. The only difference between these dormitories and prisons is that prisons mostly have solid walls, while theirs are cardboard prisons pasted with torn newspapers. Prison windows are tightly closed, while theirs are wide open. Eight or nine out of ten workers are single men with no families. When mining, they are completely naked, with only a piece of torn cloth wrapped around their abdomen, as ragged as beggars, but much dirtier. As for hygiene facilities and safety precautions in the mining area, there is no need to mention them at all. Moreover, it is our belief that if they have mortality records, we believe that the mortality rate of miners in Fu He must be able to create a new era, because the lives of the miners are constantly threatened by death. Therefore, they are superstitious about something called "Bao Huang Ye." This "Bao Huang Ye" is formed by stalactites and is located on both sides of the tunnel entrance. Before entering the tunnel to mine, they must burn incense and pray once, saying that this can prevent dizziness after entering the tunnel and ensure their safe return. This superstition cannot be understood unless we look at the workers' working environment.

In addition to tin mines, Xiwan also produces a small amount of coal. The coal mine extends westward and northward from Xiwan. The coal seam is about four to five miles long and about twenty miles wide. However, the quality of the coal in Xiwan is not very good, and the production is limited, just enough for tin smelting. Currently, there are four coal companies in Xiwan, all of which are tunnels. The coal mined is often all sand, mud, and gravel. Some cannot obtain even a jin of coal all day long. The scarcity of coal reserves can be said to be the fatal wound of Guangxi's heavy industry.

In short, the tin reserves in Fu He Zhong are very rich. Unfortunately, there are too many tin mining companies and too little capital. The government does not have a large-scale mining plan. As a result, only those small companies are allowed to use the most primitive mining tools, such as hoes, shovels, and chisels, to dig around in a chaotic manner. There is no system or plan. They mine some places with rich tin sand and abandon those with less tin sand halfway, splitting the best ore deposits into pieces, a complete mess. The places that have been mined and are deeply sunken are not filled in, and the excavated soil is piled up like mountains. It is like a piece of fatty meat, riddled with sores. When the ore is exhausted in the future, it will be impossible to restore the farmland to plant crops. The authorities cannot shirk their full responsibility for how to remedy this shortcoming.

We stayed in Babu for four days and left Babu on October 14th, taking a car back to Ping Le, and then taking a boat from Ping Le to Wuzhou. When the river water rises in May, June, July, August, and September from Ping Le to Wuzhou, electric boats can pass and reach in two days. However, in winter and spring, when the water dries up, there are many shoals and the current is rapid, only civilian boats can travel. Downstream boats take at least four days, and upstream boats take twice as long. When we returned to Ping Le, it was the time when the water was dry, and the electric boats were no longer accessible, so we had to take a civilian boat and let it go slowly. The cabins of these civilian boats are very small. The width of the boat is just enough for one person to sleep. The awning is low, and the waist cannot be straightened. We can only lie down or sit diagonally all day long. Sometimes, we occasionally run to the bow of the boat to stretch our waists, look at the green mountains and green water, and listen to the boatman rowing. This kind of time passed for four days before we were brought to Wuzhou.

As we said before, Wuzhou is "the Shanghai of Guangxi," the gathering place for import and export trade in Guangxi (as well as Yunnan and Guizhou). In recent years, import trade has greatly declined due to the bankruptcy of rural areas and the reduction of farmers' purchasing power. Export trade has been hit harder by the world economic panic, becoming even more unbearable. Under the double attack of rural decline and world panic, Wuzhou has become a scapegoat. When we stayed in Wuzhou, we heard cries of sorrow every day in individual conversations with merchants, in the Chamber of Commerce, and among factory owners and workers. They were all admiring the past, vaguely looking forward to the future, and disappointed in the present. The largest commercial firms in Wuzhou are Ping Ma Hang and Shui Mian Hang (agents who buy and sell on behalf of customers, that is, the so-called brokers in the north). These two firms have been hit hardest in recent years. For example, in terms of export goods, the major exports of Guangxi are tung oil, raw oil, and rice. In recent years, except for tung oil, which still has annual exports (estimated at about 100,000 dan last year, compared to 150,000 dan in the 16th and 17th years of the Republic of China, a decrease of about one-third), other products such as raw oil have been affected by Shandong raw oil, and the Hong Kong market has been completely occupied by Qingzhou oil. Since the 20th year, a large amount of foreign rice has been imported every year. The export of grain and rice has also been unable to withstand the impact of foreign rice dumping, and its sales in provincial markets have gradually narrowed, making it unable to gain a foothold. Of course, these goods are not produced locally in Wuzhou. They come from the Liuzhou, Fuhe, and Yonghe producing areas. Recently, the number of goods coming has indeed decreased, but even this small amount of inventory cannot find sales. When we traveled in Liuzhou, Guilin, Ping Le, etc., when asked about the reasons for the decrease in the export of local products by merchants, their only answer was "There is no price in Wuzhou." Now that we have arrived in Wuzhou, the answer we get is "There is no price in Hong Kong or Guangzhou." "No price" has destroyed Guangxi's export trade. Isn't this the best microcosm of falling prices and the world economic panic? Other things such as the heavy exploitation of miscellaneous taxes, the difficulty of transportation, and the high cost of living have all driven merchants into the abyss of despair.

Chu Minyi Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday to Discuss: Panchen Lama's Difficult Entry into Tibet Resolved; Ariyoshi's Visit to Beijing Did Not Discuss Sino-Japanese Issues

According to the Central News Agency, Chu Minyi, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing at 7:20 yesterday morning and went to the Sino-French Institute of Technology to handle school affairs. Transporting Antiquities to Beijing to Build a Storage Facility

Mr. Chu first talked about the affairs of the Palace Museum. As for the position of Secretary-General of the Palace Museum, it was assumed by Ye Chucang, Secretary-General of the Central Party Headquarters. Because Mr. Ye has many affairs, he requested to serve concurrently. Therefore, when meeting with Mr. Ma, he discussed the matter in detail. As for the convening of the council of the museum, it is still in preparation. Because the council members are scattered all over the country, it is more difficult to gather them. Therefore, ordinary matters are decided by the meeting of the standing council members. The authorities of the museum,

In view of the fact that the storage of antiquities in Shanghai requires monthly expenses of 20,000 yuan, they all advocate building a museum in the Nanjing Mausoleum. The estimated cost is 1 million yuan, which will be borrowed from the British, French, and American Boxer Indemnity funds. Also, because the construction cost of the museum is huge, it is planned to build a museum storage facility first and then expand it. However, it is learned that people in Shanghai, such as Shi Liangcai, advocate building an antiquity storage facility in Shanghai to save expenses. It is still under discussion.

According to the doctor, the Lama's tooth root has a lot of pus and needs surgery to remove it all before he can recover. Therefore, he still needs to stay in Shanghai for treatment. As for the difficult entry into Tibet, it has now been completely resolved. Reuters previously reported that the commander-in-chief of Tibet, Long Mai'er, was killed. He personally knew that the Dalai Lama had a favorite minister. He was originally a gardener, but after being appreciated by the Dalai Lama, he gained the Dalai Lama's trust with his intelligence, so he arbitrarily exercised power. It is not yet possible to verify whether this person is the murdered Long Mai'er. In short, the obstacles have been removed, and all the people in Tibet warmly welcome the Panchen Lama to enter Tibet to preside over the government. Therefore, the Panchen Lama can start soon for Tibet.

Difficult to Know the Truth About News from Southern Xinjiang

The Xinjiang Construction Committee is currently holding group meetings. The date of the general meeting has not yet been decided. As for the recent situation in southern Xinjiang, due to transportation reasons, no reports have been received recently. However, it is learned that Ma Zhongying has now failed and cannot rise again. The province is located on the border, with a vast area and rich products, so there are many coveters. Japan, Russia, England, Turkey, and other countries are all eyeing it and monitoring each other. The successive rebellions in Xinjiang must have a considerable background. However, we do not know the situation because of the lack of communication. The various telegrams have their own functions and make self-interested propaganda to serve their own interests. Therefore, the news published in various newspapers is difficult to know the truth because of this relationship. Therefore, when we read the newspaper, we should first pay attention to the source of the telegram and collect telegrams from various parties for verification, then we should know the truth slightly.

He did not undertake any mission. What the Japanese said should not be believed. The Japanese have repeatedly fabricated rumors, which are well known to the world. Seven Types of Bonds, Including Austrian Indemnity Bonds, Drawn for Principal Repayment Yesterday Morning: Principal Repayment of 2,361,000 Yuan; Austrian Payments Start at the End of This Month, 20th of the Month

The lottery for the repayment of principal of seven types of bonds, including Austrian Indemnity Secured 24 Treasury Bonds, was held by the Ministry of Finance at the Bank Association Meeting Hall on Hong Kong Road at 10:00 yesterday morning. 京滬路　附掛萬國臥車　鐵道部重訂合同

Central News Agency reports, the International Sleeping Car Company operated sleeping cars attached to the Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai) Railway. The original contract for this was established between the Railway Ministry and the company. That old contract expired at the end of May this year. The Traffic Departments of the two railway bureaus drafted a new contract, submitted it to the Railway Ministry for approval, and signed it directly with the company on May 31. It took effect on June 1. The new contract originally had 20 articles, and the key points are excerpted as follows: (1) The company (referred to as the "International Sleeping Car Company" below) is permitted to attach one sleeping car to each train of the fifth and sixth Beijing-Shanghai night express trains of this bureau. During the validity of this contract, these two trains will not be permitted to attach sleeping cars from other sleeping car companies. (2) The two sleeping cars provided by the company, each can accommodate 16 to 18 passengers. These sleeping cars remain the property of the company, but the railway bureau has the technical right to inspect whether they meet the standards. (3) All equipment for the sleeping cars, except for damage caused by the railway bureau's fault, which will be repaired by the railway bureau, natural wear and tear will be the responsibility of the company to provide materials for the railway bureau to repair. The responsibilities for the inspection and maintenance of the equipment on the cars at ordinary times shall be borne by both parties as follows: (A) The company shall be responsible for: 1. Maintaining the good condition of the car body (including car body paint and cleaning), and the color of the sleeping car shall be the same as that of the railway bureau's sleeping cars. 2. Cleaning and disinfection of the sleeping cars. 3. All precautions inside the car when the train is running. 4. Supply of bedding, washbasins, towels, and other items. (B) The railway bureau shall be responsible for: 1. All matters relating to the connection, maintenance, and repair of the top, bottom, corridors, and connecting drawhooks of the passenger cars, as well as the external steam pipes. 2. Axle lubrication, supply of oil and cotton, and cleaning en route. (4) The railway bureau shall provide free fuel for all internal heating equipment on the cars, but the company shall be responsible for the equipment and all maintenance costs of the heating equipment. When traveling or parked at the starting and ending stations, the electricity stored on the cars must be replenished, which the railway bureau will provide for free. The railway bureau shall provide free water for the cars. The railway bureau shall set up a small warehouse for the company at each starting and ending station for storing emergency materials. Except for special reasons, the railway bureau shall treat the company's sleeping cars the same as the railway bureau's vehicles. (5) The berth fares for the sleeping cars are set at 7 yuan per night for first-class A berths and 5 yuan per night for first-class B berths. If the railway bureau increases passenger fares in the future, the company may also increase fares proportionally. (6) 80% of the sleeping car revenue will go to the company, and 20% will go to the railway bureau. Settlements will be made monthly. (7) When the sleeping cars are repaired, the railway bureau shall decide and implement the repair methods and material quality. The railway bureau shall not be responsible for damage to the sleeping cars due to fire or other unavoidable and irresistible accidents. (8) The company shall pay for the hiring of various service personnel on the sleeping cars. (9) The company may send one employee to handle business and represent the company to contact the railway bureau at any time. (10) The attendants employed by the company must be of Chinese nationality. If the railway bureau considers such attendants unsuitable, it may request immediate dismissal, and the company must comply immediately. (11) Attendants must strictly abide by all laws and orders of the railway bureau. (12) The company's regulations for the management of attendants must not conflict with the railway bureau's regulations. (13) Attendants must wear service badges when on duty. These service badges shall be issued by the company and countersigned by the railway bureau. (14) The railway bureau's section chiefs, ticket inspectors, and other officials may directly enter the company's sleeping cars to perform their duties. (15) Passengers traveling in the company's sleeping cars must hold first-class passenger tickets from the railway bureau. (16) With the approval of the railway bureau, the company may transmit free telegrams regarding traffic and berth reservations. (17) In the event of disputes over the terms of the contract, both parties shall each appoint one arbitrator to resolve the matter. If the matter still cannot be resolved, the circumstances shall be stated in a memorandum and sent to the chairman of the International Railway Association, who shall appoint a third arbitrator to form an arbitration committee to decide by a majority vote. (18) This contract shall take effect from the date of signing by both parties (the old contract shall be void at the same time) and shall expire on May 31, 1936. If the sleeping car is out of service for reasons not attributable to the company, the term of validity may be extended according to the date of the outage.
